That makes daily memory files, daily session reset, and usage summaries disagree with each other.\\n- Why it matters: users experience this as \\u0026#34;the system got the date wrong\\u0026#34; even when the raw timestamps are technically correct. Session-memory files can land on the wrong day, daily reset can roll over at the host timezone instead of the user\\u0026#39;s timezone, and `/usage cost` can report a different \\u0026#34;Today\\u0026#34; than the usage bucket summary.\\n- What changed: introduced a shared \\u0026#34;human day\\u0026#34; helper and applied it to all user-facing daily boundary logic covered by this PR.\\n- What did NOT change (scope boundary): no config schema changes, no protocol/storage timestamp changes, no cron scheduling changes, no log-display changes, and no model-prompt copy changes.\\n\\n## Core idea: Human Day\\n\\nThis PR adds a small shared abstraction for the **human day**: the calendar day as experienced by the user, using the existing `agents.defaults.userTimezone` with host-timezone fallback.\\n\\nThe goal is not to replace UTC everywhere. The goal is to make all **user-facing daily boundary decisions** answer the same question the same way:\\n\\n\\u0026gt; \\u0026#34;For this user, what day is it?\\u0026#34;\\n\\nThat daily-boundary logic now lives in one place instead of being reimplemented ad hoc with `toISOString()`, host-local `setHours()`, or `toLocaleDateString()`.\\n\\n## What changed\\n\\n### Shared helper\\n\\nAdded `src/infra/format-time/human-day.ts` with shared helpers for:\\n\\n- resolving the human timezone from existing config\\n- formatting a `YYYY-MM-DD` day key for that timezone\\n- formatting local wall-clock time for human-facing daily artifacts\\n- resolving the daily reset cycle key/boundary in that timezone\\n\\n### Session memory\\n\\nUpdated `src/hooks/bundled/session-memory/handler.ts`:\\n\\n- session-memory filenames now use the human day instead of UTC date slicing\\n- fallback HHMM slug now uses human local time instead of UTC time\\n- markdown header now shows the human local time and timezone label\\n- the memory file date is based on the previous session\\u0026#39;s `updatedAt` when available, which better matches \\u0026#34;the day this session actually belonged to\\u0026#34; than UTC event time\\n\\nThis fixes the class of bug where a late-night session in `Asia/Shanghai` gets stored as the previous UTC date.\\n\\n### Session reset\\n\\nUpdated `src/config/sessions/reset.ts` and its callers so daily freshness is evaluated using the human-day reset cycle instead of host-local `Date#setHours()`.\\n\\nThis means `session.reset.atHour` now behaves consistently with the configured user timezone for daily rollover decisions.\\n\\n### Usage daily buckets\\n\\nUpdated same day-key logic as the bucket summary.\\n\\n### Memory flush\\n\\nUpdated `src/auto-reply/reply/memory-flush.ts` so the canonical `memory/YYYY-MM-DD.md` path uses the same shared human-day helper.\\n\\n## Why this approach\\n\\nThis PR intentionally fixes one specific class of time bugs:\\n\\n- **user-facing daily boundary logic**\\n\\nIt does **not** try to solve every timezone-related behavior in one shot.\\n\\nThat separation is deliberate:\\n\\n- raw transcript / protocol timestamps should remain UTC\\n- cron scheduling has its own semantics and should stay separate\\n- log display defaults are a separate UX topic\\n\\nKeeping this PR centered on **human-day semantics** makes the behavior easier to reason about and the scope easier to review.\\n\\n## User-visible behavior changes\\n\\n- Session-memory files now land on the user\\u0026#39;s calendar day instead of the UTC day.\\n- Session-memory markdown headers now show local time with timezone label.\\n- Daily session reset now follows the user\\u0026#39;s calendar day instead of the gateway host\\u0026#39;s local day.\\n- Usage daily buckets and `/usage cost` now agree on what counts as `Today`.\\n- Memory flush canonical daily path now matches the same day-boundary logic.\\n\\n## Security impact\\n\\n- New permissions/capabilities? There is no atomic update/replace operation, which creates a data-loss window: if an agent calls `memory_forget` and then `memory_store` in sequence and the store fails, the original memory is gone with nothing to replace it.\\n\\nAdditionally, there is no way to preview similar memories before storing, so agents can\\u0026#39;t detect conflicts before overwriting.\\n\\n## Solution\\n\\nThis PR adds a **`memory_refresh` tool** that operates in two modes:\\n\\n### Mode 1 — Search-only (no `memoryId`)\\n\\nCall with only `text` to preview similar memories before committing:\\n- Embeds `text` using the same model as `memory_recall`\\n- Searches LanceDB for top 3 similar entries (with cosine similarity scores)\\n- Returns matches **without storing anything**\\n- Agent reviews and decides whether to call again with a `memoryId` to replace\\n\\n```json\\n{ \\u0026#34;operation\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;search_only\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;matches\\u0026#34;: [{ \\u0026#34;id\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;text\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;category\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;importance\\u0026#34;: 0.8, \\u0026#34;similarity\\u0026#34;: 0.93 }] }\\n```\\n\\n### Mode 2 — Atomic replace (`memoryId` provided)\\n\\nAtomically replaces a specific memory:\\n1. Reads the existing entry (captures old text for audit)\\n2. Deletes the old entry\\n3. Inserts the new entry with `text`/`category`/`importance`\\n4. On insert failure: **best-effort rollback** restores the original (returns `rollbackWarning` in result)\\n5. Appends to audit log at `~/.openclaw/memory/refresh-audit.jsonl`\\n\\n```json\\n{ \\u0026#34;operation\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;replaced\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;old_id\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;new_id\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;old_text_preview\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;first 80 chars\\u0026#34; }\\n```\\n\\n### Audit log\\n\\nEvery Mode 2 operation appends a JSONL line to `~/.openclaw/memory/refresh-audit.jsonl` (created if absent):\\n\\n```json\\n{\\u0026#34;ts\\u0026#34;: 1234567890, \\u0026#34;operation\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;replaced\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;old_id\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;new_id\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;similarity\\u0026#34;: 0.95, \\u0026#34;old_text\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;first 80 chars\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;new_text\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;first 80 chars\\u0026#34;}\\n```\\n\\nNo audit entry is written for Mode 1 (search-only).\\n\\n## Changes\\n\\n- **`extensions/memory-lancedb/index.ts`**\\n  - Added `node:fs/promises`, `node:os`, `node:path` imports\\n  - Added `MemoryDB.getById(id)` using LanceDB filter query (`table.query().where(...).toArray()`)\\n  - Registered `memory_refresh` tool following the exact same pattern as the other three tools\\n\\n- **`extensions/memory-lancedb/index.test.ts`**\\n  - Updated live test tool count: 3 → 4\\n  - Added 4 unit tests (all mocked, no OpenAI key required):\\n    1. Search-only mode: returns top 3 matches with similarity, does NOT call `add`/`delete`\\n    2. Atomic replace: old entry deleted, new entry added, audit log written\\n    3. Non-existent `memoryId`: returns `error: not_found`, nothing written or deleted\\n    4. Best-effort rollback: when `add` fails, original is restored via second `add` call\\n\\n## Test results\\n\\n```\\n✓ extensions/memory-lancedb/index.test.ts (17 tests | 1 skipped) 123ms\\n  16 passed | 1 skipped (live test — needs OPENAI_API_KEY)\\n```\\n\\n## Related\\n\\nComplementary to #21003 (`memory_write`/upsert for file-based memory) — that PR covers the markdown/file memory system; this PR covers the LanceDB vector memory system. The session store (`sessions.json`) survives on disk, but `waitForSubagentCompletion` → `agent.wait` RPC fails silently (or returns a spurious `\\u0026#39;timeout\\u0026#39;` status) because the agent process is gone — causing a false failure cascade. Runs that actually completed never deliver their results.\\n\\n## What this PR does (Phase 1)\\n\\nThree targeted changes in `src/agents/`:\\n\\n### Change 1: `rehydrateSessionStoreEntries()` — `subagent-resume.ts`\\n\\nCalled in `restoreSubagentRunsOnce()` **before** `reconcileOrphanedRestoredRuns()` so the orphan check sees a populated store entry.\\n\\nFor in-flight registry entries whose session-store entry is missing:\\n1. Force a cache-bypassing re-read of `sessions.json` (handles the case where the store was written but the in-memory cache is stale)\\n2. If still missing, scan the agent\\u0026#39;s sessions directory for a `.jsonl` transcript created within 5 minutes of the registry entry\\u0026#39;s `createdAt`\\n3. If exactly one candidate is found, read its `{type:\\u0026#39;session\\u0026#39;}` header to extract the `sessionId`, then write a minimal synthetic store entry: `{ sessionId, updatedAt, sessionFile, spawnedBy, spawnDepth: 1 }`\\n\\nThis prevents false `\\u0026#39;missing-session-entry\\u0026#39;` orphan conclusions for the ~400ms race window between spawn and first store write.\\n\\n### Change 2: `resolveSubagentRunResumability()` — `subagent-resume.ts`\\n\\nReplaces the binary orphan/no-orphan check with a **4-way classification**:\\n\\n| State | Condition | Recovery action |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| `resumable-announce-only` | `endedAt` is already set | Retry announce delivery (already handled) |\\n| `resumable-replay` | Session-store entry exists, transcript has ≥1 assistant turn, no `endedAt` | Capture result from transcript, call `completeSubagentRun` |\\n| `resumable-fresh` | Session-store entry exists, transcript is empty/header-only, no `endedAt` | Re-dispatch original task via `callGateway(\\u0026#39;agent\\u0026#39;)` |\\n| `orphaned` | No session-store entry AND no recoverable transcript | Existing orphan-pruning behaviour |\\n\\n### Change 3: `resumeSubagentRun()` routing — `subagent-registry.ts`\\n\\nModified to call `routeResumedRun()` (which calls `resolveSubagentRunResumability()`) before falling through to the default `waitForSubagentCompletion` path:\\n\\n- **`resumable-replay`**: calls `completeSubagentRun` directly with `{ status: \\u0026#39;ok\\u0026#39; }`, which uses the existing `freezeRunResultAtCompletion` → `captureSubagentCompletionReply` flow to read the transcript result and trigger the announce flow. No `agent.wait` call needed.\\n- **`resumable-fresh`**: re-dispatches the original task to the child session via `callGateway(\\u0026#39;agent\\u0026#39;)` (new idempotency key), waits with `agent.wait` on the **new** run ID, then calls `completeSubagentRun` for the **original** run entry.\\n- **`orphaned`** / **`resumable-announce-only`**: unchanged — routed by existing logic.\\n\\n## What Phase 2 will cover (not in this PR)\\n\\n- Synthetic `tool_result` injection for partially-completed transcripts (to avoid re-running from scratch when the agent was mid-tool-call)\\n- `SIGTERM` checkpointing to write a graceful shutdown marker to the transcript\\n- Per-run max-resume caps to prevent infinite retry loops on pathological transcripts\\n\\n## Tests\\n\\n25 new unit tests in `src/agents/subagent-resume.test.ts`:\\n- `readTranscriptSessionId` — 5 cases (valid header, missing file, wrong type, empty, malformed JSON)\\n- `transcriptHasAssistantTurn` — 6 cases (has assistant, header only, user only, missing, empty, malformed + valid)\\n- `resolveSubagentRunResumability` — 7 cases covering all 4 classifications\\n- `rehydrateSessionStoreEntries` — skip completed, skip existing, synthesise from transcript\\n- `routeResumedRun` — orphaned → false, announce-only → false, replay → true, fresh → true\\n\\n## References\\n\\nCloses #27875\\nRelated: #19780, #20436\",\"state\":\"open\",\"draft\":false,\"merged\":false,\"html_url\":\"https://github.com/openclaw/openclaw/pull/43497\",\"user\":{\"login\":\"amittell\",\"id\":1388680,\"profile_url\":\"https://github.com/amittell\",\"avatar_url\":\"https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/1388680?v=4\"},\"labels\":[\"agents\",\"size: XL\"],\"head\":{\"ref\":\"feat/subagent-restart-resume-phase1\",\"sha\":\"264e3909462e062fbe001ba652ff095e33595423\",\"repo\":{\"full_name\":\"amittell/openclaw\",\"description\":\"Your own personal AI assistant. The subsequent files each arrive as independent messages and trigger separate agent turns — or worse, are silently ignored because the agent is still processing the first one.\\n\\n**User-visible symptom:**\\n\\u0026gt; \\u0026#34;제온아 이거 세션 6개를 한번에 다 읽고 요약해줘\\u0026#34; → only Session 01 received; sessions 02–06 dropped.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Root Cause\\n\\nTelegram\\u0026#39;s Bot API distinguishes between two kinds of multi-file sends:\\n\\n| What user sends | Bot API behavior | `media_group_id` present? |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| Multiple **photos/videos** selected together | Sent as a media group | ✅ Yes |\\n| Multiple **documents** (`.md`, `.pdf`, `.txt`, …) selected together | Sent as **individual, separate messages** | ❌ No |\\n\\nOpenClaw\\u0026#39;s existing `processMediaGroup` handler (in `src/channels/telegram/reply.ts`) correctly collapses Telegram media groups using `media_group_id`. However, document files — the most common use case for \\u0026#34;send me all these files\\u0026#34; workflows — **never carry `media_group_id`** and fall through to individual `processMessage` calls.\\n\\n### Relevant code path\\n\\n```typescript\\n// Current: media_group_id grouping only\\nconst mediaGroupId = msg.media_group_id;\\nif (mediaGroupId) {\\n  // ✅ Photos/videos: correctly batched\\n  const existing = mediaGroupBuffer.get(mediaGroupId);\\n  // ... collect and flush after MEDIA_GROUP_TIMEOUT_MS (500ms)\\n  return;\\n}\\n\\n// ❌ Documents land here — each triggers a separate processMessage\\nlet media = null;\\ntry {\\n  media = await resolveMedia(ctx, mediaMaxBytes, opts.token, opts.proxyFetch);\\n} catch { ... }\\nawait processMessage(ctx, media ? [media] : [], storeAllowFrom, ...);\\n```\\n\\nNote: OpenClaw **already implements** a similar batching pattern for split text messages (`textFragmentBuffer` / `TELEGRAM_TEXT_FRAGMENT_MAX_GAP_MS`). The same pattern can be extended to document files.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Proposed Solution\\n\\nIntroduce a **per-chat document buffer** that collects document messages from the same sender within a short flush window, then dispatches them as a single `processMessage` call — mirroring the existing `mediaGroupBuffer` and `textFragmentBuffer` patterns.\\n\\n### Implementation sketch\\n\\n```typescript\\n// New constant (tune as needed)\\nconst DOCUMENT_BATCH_TIMEOUT_MS = 1500; // 1.5 s window\\n\\n// New buffer (alongside existing mediaGroupBuffer, textFragmentBuffer)\\ntype DocumentBatchEntry = {\\n  messages: Array\\u0026lt;{ msg: Message; ctx: Context }\\u0026gt;;\\n  timer: ReturnType;\\n  key: string; // `${chatId}:${senderId}`\\n};\\nconst documentBatchBuffer = new Map();\\nlet documentBatchProcessing = Promise.resolve();\\n\\n// New flush function\\nconst processDocumentBatch = async (entry: DocumentBatchEntry) =\\u0026gt; {\\n  entry.messages.sort((a, b) =\\u0026gt; a.msg.message_id - b.msg.message_id);\\n  const primaryEntry = entry.messages.find(m =\\u0026gt; m.msg.caption || m.msg.text) ?? entry.messages[0];\\n  const allMedia: ResolvedMedia[] = [];\\n\\n  for (const { ctx } of entry.messages) {\\n    try {\\n      const media = await resolveMedia(ctx, mediaMaxBytes, opts.token, opts.proxyFetch);\\n      if (media) allMedia.push({ path: media.path, contentType: media.contentType });\\n    } catch (err) {\\n      runtime.log?.(warn(`document batch: skipping file that failed to fetch: ${String(err)}`));\\n    }\\n  }\\n\\n  const storeAllowFrom = await loadStoreAllowFrom();\\n  const replyMedia = await resolveReplyMediaForMessage(primaryEntry.ctx, primaryEntry.msg);\\n  await processMessage(primaryEntry.ctx, allMedia, storeAllowFrom, undefined, replyMedia);\\n};\\n\\n// Hook into the existing single-message flow, before processMessage is called:\\nif (!mediaGroupId \\u0026amp;\\u0026amp; msg.document) {\\n  const key = `${chatId}:${String(senderId)}`;\\n  const existing = documentBatchBuffer.get(key);\\n  if (existing) {\\n    clearTimeout(existing.timer);\\n    existing.messages.push({ msg, ctx });\\n    existing.timer = setTimeout(async () =\\u0026gt; {\\n      documentBatchBuffer.delete(key);\\n      documentBatchProcessing = documentBatchProcessing.then(async () =\\u0026gt; {\\n        await processDocumentBatch(existing);\\n      }).catch(() =\\u0026gt; void 0);\\n      await documentBatchProcessing;\\n    }, DOCUMENT_BATCH_TIMEOUT_MS);\\n  } else {\\n    const entry: DocumentBatchEntry = {\\n      key,\\n      messages: [{ msg, ctx }],\\n      timer: setTimeout(async () =\\u0026gt; {\\n        documentBatchBuffer.delete(key);\\n        documentBatchProcessing = documentBatchProcessing.then(async () =\\u0026gt; {\\n          await processDocumentBatch(entry);\\n        }).catch(() =\\u0026gt; void 0);\\n        await documentBatchProcessing;\\n      }, DOCUMENT_BATCH_TIMEOUT_MS),\\n    };\\n    documentBatchBuffer.set(key, entry);\\n  }\\n  return; // defer until flush\\n}\\n```\\n\\n### Config option (optional, for power users)\\n\\n```jsonc\\n// openclaw.json\\n{\\n  \\u0026#34;channels\\u0026#34;: {\\n    \\u0026#34;telegram\\u0026#34;: {\\n      \\u0026#34;documentBatchWindowMs\\u0026#34;: 1500  // 0 to disable batching\\n    }\\n  }\\n}\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Why 1.5 s?\\n\\n- Telegram\\u0026#39;s own delivery jitter for documents is typically 200–800 ms between successive files.\\n- The existing `MEDIA_GROUP_TIMEOUT_MS` is 500 ms (sufficient because `media_group_id` messages arrive in a tight burst from the server).\\n- Documents are sent one-by-one by the client, so a wider window is needed. 1.5 s covers the typical user experience of tapping \\u0026#34;select all + send\\u0026#34; on mobile.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Files to change\\n\\n| File | Change |\\n|---|---|\\n| `src/channels/telegram/reply.ts` | Add `documentBatchBuffer` + `processDocumentBatch` (mirrors `mediaGroupBuffer` / `processMediaGroup`) |\\n| `src/channels/telegram/config.ts` | Add optional `documentBatchWindowMs` config field (default `1500`) |\\n| `src/channels/telegram/reply.test.ts` | Add tests: single doc passes through immediately after flush; multiple docs from same sender within window arrive as one `processMessage` call |\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Testing\\n\\n```\\n# Manual: send 3 .md files in quick succession in Telegram\\n# Expected: agent receives all 3 as a single inbound turn with allMedia.length === 3\\n\\n# Unit test (existing test timing infrastructure already supports testTimings.mediaGroupFlushMs)\\n# Extend with: testTimings.documentBatchFlushMs\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Non-goals\\n\\n- This PR does **not** change how `media_group_id` messages (photos/videos) are handled — that logic is already correct.\\n- This PR does **not** introduce cross-chat or cross-sender batching — the buffer key is always `${chatId}:${senderId}`.\\n\\n---\\n\\n*Discovered by: Simon Kim (@simonkim_nft) / Zeon · 2026-03-04*\\n\",\"state\":\"open\",\"draft\":false,\"merged\":false,\"html_url\":\"https://github.com/openclaw/openclaw/pull/34942\",\"user\":{\"login\":\"seojoonkim\",\"id\":2534327,\"profile_url\":\"https://github.com/seojoonkim\",\"avatar_url\":\"https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/2534327?v=4\"},\"labels\":[\"docs\",\"channel: telegram\",\"extensions: google-antigravity-auth\",\"cli\",\"scripts\",\"agents\",\"size: L\"],\"head\":{\"ref\":\"feat/batch-document-attachments\",\"sha\":\"62915a7e8d067d9f772dfdc54a6864ca40c64b6b\",\"repo\":{\"full_name\":\"seojoonkim/moltbot\",\"description\":\"Your own personal AI assistant. There is no atomic update/replace operation, which creates a data-loss window: if an agent calls `memory_forget` and then `memory_store` in sequence and the store fails, the original memory is gone with nothing to replace it.\\n\\nAdditionally, there is no way to preview similar memories before storing, so agents can\\u0026#39;t detect conflicts before overwriting.\\n\\n## Solution\\n\\nThis PR adds a **`memory_refresh` tool** that operates in two modes:\\n\\n### Mode 1 — Search-only (no `memoryId`)\\n\\nCall with only `text` to preview similar memories before committing:\\n- Embeds `text` using the same model as `memory_recall`\\n- Searches LanceDB for top 3 similar entries (with cosine similarity scores)\\n- Returns matches **without storing anything**\\n- Agent reviews and decides whether to call again with a `memoryId` to replace\\n\\n```json\\n{ \\u0026#34;operation\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;search_only\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;matches\\u0026#34;: [{ \\u0026#34;id\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;text\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;category\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;importance\\u0026#34;: 0.8, \\u0026#34;similarity\\u0026#34;: 0.93 }] }\\n```\\n\\n### Mode 2 — Atomic replace (`memoryId` provided)\\n\\nAtomically replaces a specific memory:\\n1. Reads the existing entry (captures old text for audit)\\n2. Deletes the old entry\\n3. Inserts the new entry with `text`/`category`/`importance`\\n4. On insert failure: **best-effort rollback** restores the original (returns `rollbackWarning` in result)\\n5. Appends to audit log at `~/.openclaw/memory/refresh-audit.jsonl`\\n\\n```json\\n{ \\u0026#34;operation\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;replaced\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;old_id\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;new_id\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;old_text_preview\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;first 80 chars\\u0026#34; }\\n```\\n\\n### Audit log\\n\\nEvery Mode 2 operation appends a JSONL line to `~/.openclaw/memory/refresh-audit.jsonl` (created if absent):\\n\\n```json\\n{\\u0026#34;ts\\u0026#34;: 1234567890, \\u0026#34;operation\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;replaced\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;old_id\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;new_id\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;similarity\\u0026#34;: 0.95, \\u0026#34;old_text\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;first 80 chars\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;new_text\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;first 80 chars\\u0026#34;}\\n```\\n\\nNo audit entry is written for Mode 1 (search-only).\\n\\n## Changes\\n\\n- **`extensions/memory-lancedb/index.ts`**\\n  - Added `node:fs/promises`, `node:os`, `node:path` imports\\n  - Added `MemoryDB.getById(id)` using LanceDB filter query (`table.query().where(...).toArray()`)\\n  - Registered `memory_refresh` tool following the exact same pattern as the other three tools\\n\\n- **`extensions/memory-lancedb/index.test.ts`**\\n  - Updated live test tool count: 3 → 4\\n  - Added 4 unit tests (all mocked, no OpenAI key required):\\n    1. Search-only mode: returns top 3 matches with similarity, does NOT call `add`/`delete`\\n    2. Atomic replace: old entry deleted, new entry added, audit log written\\n    3. Non-existent `memoryId`: returns `error: not_found`, nothing written or deleted\\n    4. Best-effort rollback: when `add` fails, original is restored via second `add` call\\n\\n## Test results\\n\\n```\\n✓ extensions/memory-lancedb/index.test.ts (17 tests | 1 skipped) 123ms\\n  16 passed | 1 skipped (live test — needs OPENAI_API_KEY)\\n```\\n\\n## Related\\n\\nComplementary to #21003 (`memory_write`/upsert for file-based memory) — that PR covers the markdown/file memory system; this PR covers the LanceDB vector memory system. The session store (`sessions.json`) survives on disk, but `waitForSubagentCompletion` → `agent.wait` RPC fails silently (or returns a spurious `\\u0026#39;timeout\\u0026#39;` status) because the agent process is gone — causing a false failure cascade. Runs that actually completed never deliver their results.\\n\\n## What this PR does (Phase 1)\\n\\nThree targeted changes in `src/agents/`:\\n\\n### Change 1: `rehydrateSessionStoreEntries()` — `subagent-resume.ts`\\n\\nCalled in `restoreSubagentRunsOnce()` **before** `reconcileOrphanedRestoredRuns()` so the orphan check sees a populated store entry.\\n\\nFor in-flight registry entries whose session-store entry is missing:\\n1. Force a cache-bypassing re-read of `sessions.json` (handles the case where the store was written but the in-memory cache is stale)\\n2. If still missing, scan the agent\\u0026#39;s sessions directory for a `.jsonl` transcript created within 5 minutes of the registry entry\\u0026#39;s `createdAt`\\n3. If exactly one candidate is found, read its `{type:\\u0026#39;session\\u0026#39;}` header to extract the `sessionId`, then write a minimal synthetic store entry: `{ sessionId, updatedAt, sessionFile, spawnedBy, spawnDepth: 1 }`\\n\\nThis prevents false `\\u0026#39;missing-session-entry\\u0026#39;` orphan conclusions for the ~400ms race window between spawn and first store write.\\n\\n### Change 2: `resolveSubagentRunResumability()` — `subagent-resume.ts`\\n\\nReplaces the binary orphan/no-orphan check with a **4-way classification**:\\n\\n| State | Condition | Recovery action |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| `resumable-announce-only` | `endedAt` is already set | Retry announce delivery (already handled) |\\n| `resumable-replay` | Session-store entry exists, transcript has ≥1 assistant turn, no `endedAt` | Capture result from transcript, call `completeSubagentRun` |\\n| `resumable-fresh` | Session-store entry exists, transcript is empty/header-only, no `endedAt` | Re-dispatch original task via `callGateway(\\u0026#39;agent\\u0026#39;)` |\\n| `orphaned` | No session-store entry AND no recoverable transcript | Existing orphan-pruning behaviour |\\n\\n### Change 3: `resumeSubagentRun()` routing — `subagent-registry.ts`\\n\\nModified to call `routeResumedRun()` (which calls `resolveSubagentRunResumability()`) before falling through to the default `waitForSubagentCompletion` path:\\n\\n- **`resumable-replay`**: calls `completeSubagentRun` directly with `{ status: \\u0026#39;ok\\u0026#39; }`, which uses the existing `freezeRunResultAtCompletion` → `captureSubagentCompletionReply` flow to read the transcript result and trigger the announce flow. No `agent.wait` call needed.\\n- **`resumable-fresh`**: re-dispatches the original task to the child session via `callGateway(\\u0026#39;agent\\u0026#39;)` (new idempotency key), waits with `agent.wait` on the **new** run ID, then calls `completeSubagentRun` for the **original** run entry.\\n- **`orphaned`** / **`resumable-announce-only`**: unchanged — routed by existing logic.\\n\\n## What Phase 2 will cover (not in this PR)\\n\\n- Synthetic `tool_result` injection for partially-completed transcripts (to avoid re-running from scratch when the agent was mid-tool-call)\\n- `SIGTERM` checkpointing to write a graceful shutdown marker to the transcript\\n- Per-run max-resume caps to prevent infinite retry loops on pathological transcripts\\n\\n## Tests\\n\\n25 new unit tests in `src/agents/subagent-resume.test.ts`:\\n- `readTranscriptSessionId` — 5 cases (valid header, missing file, wrong type, empty, malformed JSON)\\n- `transcriptHasAssistantTurn` — 6 cases (has assistant, header only, user only, missing, empty, malformed + valid)\\n- `resolveSubagentRunResumability` — 7 cases covering all 4 classifications\\n- `rehydrateSessionStoreEntries` — skip completed, skip existing, synthesise from transcript\\n- `routeResumedRun` — orphaned → false, announce-only → false, replay → true, fresh → true\\n\\n## References\\n\\nCloses #27875\\nRelated: #19780, #20436\",\"state\":\"open\",\"draft\":false,\"merged\":false,\"html_url\":\"https://github.com/openclaw/openclaw/pull/43497\",\"user\":{\"login\":\"amittell\",\"id\":1388680,\"profile_url\":\"https://github.com/amittell\",\"avatar_url\":\"https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/1388680?v=4\"},\"labels\":[\"agents\",\"size: XL\"],\"head\":{\"ref\":\"feat/subagent-restart-resume-phase1\",\"sha\":\"264e3909462e062fbe001ba652ff095e33595423\",\"repo\":{\"full_name\":\"amittell/openclaw\",\"description\":\"Your own personal AI assistant. The subsequent files each arrive as independent messages and trigger separate agent turns — or worse, are silently ignored because the agent is still processing the first one.\\n\\n**User-visible symptom:**\\n\\u0026gt; \\u0026#34;제온아 이거 세션 6개를 한번에 다 읽고 요약해줘\\u0026#34; → only Session 01 received; sessions 02–06 dropped.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Root Cause\\n\\nTelegram\\u0026#39;s Bot API distinguishes between two kinds of multi-file sends:\\n\\n| What user sends | Bot API behavior | `media_group_id` present? |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| Multiple **photos/videos** selected together | Sent as a media group | ✅ Yes |\\n| Multiple **documents** (`.md`, `.pdf`, `.txt`, …) selected together | Sent as **individual, separate messages** | ❌ No |\\n\\nOpenClaw\\u0026#39;s existing `processMediaGroup` handler (in `src/channels/telegram/reply.ts`) correctly collapses Telegram media groups using `media_group_id`. However, document files — the most common use case for \\u0026#34;send me all these files\\u0026#34; workflows — **never carry `media_group_id`** and fall through to individual `processMessage` calls.\\n\\n### Relevant code path\\n\\n```typescript\\n// Current: media_group_id grouping only\\nconst mediaGroupId = msg.media_group_id;\\nif (mediaGroupId) {\\n  // ✅ Photos/videos: correctly batched\\n  const existing = mediaGroupBuffer.get(mediaGroupId);\\n  // ... collect and flush after MEDIA_GROUP_TIMEOUT_MS (500ms)\\n  return;\\n}\\n\\n// ❌ Documents land here — each triggers a separate processMessage\\nlet media = null;\\ntry {\\n  media = await resolveMedia(ctx, mediaMaxBytes, opts.token, opts.proxyFetch);\\n} catch { ... }\\nawait processMessage(ctx, media ? [media] : [], storeAllowFrom, ...);\\n```\\n\\nNote: OpenClaw **already implements** a similar batching pattern for split text messages (`textFragmentBuffer` / `TELEGRAM_TEXT_FRAGMENT_MAX_GAP_MS`). The same pattern can be extended to document files.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Proposed Solution\\n\\nIntroduce a **per-chat document buffer** that collects document messages from the same sender within a short flush window, then dispatches them as a single `processMessage` call — mirroring the existing `mediaGroupBuffer` and `textFragmentBuffer` patterns.\\n\\n### Implementation sketch\\n\\n```typescript\\n// New constant (tune as needed)\\nconst DOCUMENT_BATCH_TIMEOUT_MS = 1500; // 1.5 s window\\n\\n// New buffer (alongside existing mediaGroupBuffer, textFragmentBuffer)\\ntype DocumentBatchEntry = {\\n  messages: Array\\u0026lt;{ msg: Message; ctx: Context }\\u0026gt;;\\n  timer: ReturnType;\\n  key: string; // `${chatId}:${senderId}`\\n};\\nconst documentBatchBuffer = new Map();\\nlet documentBatchProcessing = Promise.resolve();\\n\\n// New flush function\\nconst processDocumentBatch = async (entry: DocumentBatchEntry) =\\u0026gt; {\\n  entry.messages.sort((a, b) =\\u0026gt; a.msg.message_id - b.msg.message_id);\\n  const primaryEntry = entry.messages.find(m =\\u0026gt; m.msg.caption || m.msg.text) ?? entry.messages[0];\\n  const allMedia: ResolvedMedia[] = [];\\n\\n  for (const { ctx } of entry.messages) {\\n    try {\\n      const media = await resolveMedia(ctx, mediaMaxBytes, opts.token, opts.proxyFetch);\\n      if (media) allMedia.push({ path: media.path, contentType: media.contentType });\\n    } catch (err) {\\n      runtime.log?.(warn(`document batch: skipping file that failed to fetch: ${String(err)}`));\\n    }\\n  }\\n\\n  const storeAllowFrom = await loadStoreAllowFrom();\\n  const replyMedia = await resolveReplyMediaForMessage(primaryEntry.ctx, primaryEntry.msg);\\n  await processMessage(primaryEntry.ctx, allMedia, storeAllowFrom, undefined, replyMedia);\\n};\\n\\n// Hook into the existing single-message flow, before processMessage is called:\\nif (!mediaGroupId \\u0026amp;\\u0026amp; msg.document) {\\n  const key = `${chatId}:${String(senderId)}`;\\n  const existing = documentBatchBuffer.get(key);\\n  if (existing) {\\n    clearTimeout(existing.timer);\\n    existing.messages.push({ msg, ctx });\\n    existing.timer = setTimeout(async () =\\u0026gt; {\\n      documentBatchBuffer.delete(key);\\n      documentBatchProcessing = documentBatchProcessing.then(async () =\\u0026gt; {\\n        await processDocumentBatch(existing);\\n      }).catch(() =\\u0026gt; void 0);\\n      await documentBatchProcessing;\\n    }, DOCUMENT_BATCH_TIMEOUT_MS);\\n  } else {\\n    const entry: DocumentBatchEntry = {\\n      key,\\n      messages: [{ msg, ctx }],\\n      timer: setTimeout(async () =\\u0026gt; {\\n        documentBatchBuffer.delete(key);\\n        documentBatchProcessing = documentBatchProcessing.then(async () =\\u0026gt; {\\n          await processDocumentBatch(entry);\\n        }).catch(() =\\u0026gt; void 0);\\n        await documentBatchProcessing;\\n      }, DOCUMENT_BATCH_TIMEOUT_MS),\\n    };\\n    documentBatchBuffer.set(key, entry);\\n  }\\n  return; // defer until flush\\n}\\n```\\n\\n### Config option (optional, for power users)\\n\\n```jsonc\\n// openclaw.json\\n{\\n  \\u0026#34;channels\\u0026#34;: {\\n    \\u0026#34;telegram\\u0026#34;: {\\n      \\u0026#34;documentBatchWindowMs\\u0026#34;: 1500  // 0 to disable batching\\n    }\\n  }\\n}\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Why 1.5 s?\\n\\n- Telegram\\u0026#39;s own delivery jitter for documents is typically 200–800 ms between successive files.\\n- The existing `MEDIA_GROUP_TIMEOUT_MS` is 500 ms (sufficient because `media_group_id` messages arrive in a tight burst from the server).\\n- Documents are sent one-by-one by the client, so a wider window is needed. 1.5 s covers the typical user experience of tapping \\u0026#34;select all + send\\u0026#34; on mobile.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Files to change\\n\\n| File | Change |\\n|---|---|\\n| `src/channels/telegram/reply.ts` | Add `documentBatchBuffer` + `processDocumentBatch` (mirrors `mediaGroupBuffer` / `processMediaGroup`) |\\n| `src/channels/telegram/config.ts` | Add optional `documentBatchWindowMs` config field (default `1500`) |\\n| `src/channels/telegram/reply.test.ts` | Add tests: single doc passes through immediately after flush; multiple docs from same sender within window arrive as one `processMessage` call |\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Testing\\n\\n```\\n# Manual: send 3 .md files in quick succession in Telegram\\n# Expected: agent receives all 3 as a single inbound turn with allMedia.length === 3\\n\\n# Unit test (existing test timing infrastructure already supports testTimings.mediaGroupFlushMs)\\n# Extend with: testTimings.documentBatchFlushMs\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Non-goals\\n\\n- This PR does **not** change how `media_group_id` messages (photos/videos) are handled — that logic is already correct.\\n- This PR does **not** introduce cross-chat or cross-sender batching — the buffer key is always `${chatId}:${senderId}`.\\n\\n---\\n\\n*Discovered by: Simon Kim (@simonkim_nft) / Zeon · 2026-03-04*\\n\",\"state\":\"open\",\"draft\":false,\"merged\":false,\"html_url\":\"https://github.com/openclaw/openclaw/pull/34942\",\"user\":{\"login\":\"seojoonkim\",\"id\":2534327,\"profile_url\":\"https://github.com/seojoonkim\",\"avatar_url\":\"https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/2534327?v=4\"},\"labels\":[\"docs\",\"channel: telegram\",\"extensions: google-antigravity-auth\",\"cli\",\"scripts\",\"agents\",\"size: L\"],\"head\":{\"ref\":\"feat/batch-document-attachments\",\"sha\":\"62915a7e8d067d9f772dfdc54a6864ca40c64b6b\",\"repo\":{\"full_name\":\"seojoonkim/moltbot\",\"description\":\"Your own personal AI assistant.
